  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText6270158585401203167" style="display:none">For sixteen-year-old Charlotte Reynolds, aka Charlie, being raised by a single dad and three older brothers has its perks. She can outrun, outscore, and outwit every boy she knows—including her longtime neighbor and honorary fourth brother, Braden. But when it comes to being a girl, Charlie doesn't know the first thing about anything. So when she starts working at chichi boutique to pay off a speeding ticket, she finds herself in a strange new world of makeup, lacy skirts, and BeDazzlers. Even stranger, she's spending time with a boy who has never seen her tear it up in a pickup game.<br /><br />To cope with the stress of faking her way through this new reality, Charlie seeks late-night refuge in her backyard, talking out her problems with Braden by the fence that separates them. But their Fence Chats can't solve Charlie's biggest problem: she's falling for Braden. Hard. She knows what it means to go for the win, but if spilling her secret means losing him for good, the stakes just got too high.</span>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">For all of you hating you probably do not understand what picture she was trying to paint. I understand because I have brothers and I used to be a tom<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">For all of you hating you probably do not understand what picture she was trying to paint. I understand because I have brothers and I used to be a tomboy and play football and everything with them and their friends but then I got peer pressured into being a girly girl, and I got the exact same reaction from my brothers and their friends. I realized I was changing myself and I really related with Charlie. This story is so good, and if you want action do not read a love story. It was amazing and eventful and so cute I loved the book. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6198407363420062683">Kasie West and I are NOT FRIENDS.<br/><br/>Normally at the beginning of a review like this, I would write something like “Kasie West and I have a complicated relationship.” But it’s not that complicated. It’s mostly that she keeps writing books with charming synopses and cute covers, and I keep getting sucked in and then not liking them and swearing up and down that I’m done with Kasie West, and then she writes another seemingly cute and charming book and I’m right back on the bandwagon.<br/><br/>This book, for a l</span>
  <span id="freeText6198407363420062683" style="display:none">Kasie West and I are NOT FRIENDS.<br /><br />Normally at the beginning of a review like this, I would write something like “Kasie West and I have a complicated relationship.” But it’s not that complicated. It’s mostly that she keeps writing books with charming synopses and cute covers, and I keep getting sucked in and then not liking them and swearing up and down that I’m done with Kasie West, and then she writes another seemingly cute and charming book and I’m right back on the bandwagon.<br /><br />This book, for a long time, has been the outlier. This was my first Kasie West book, and also one of the first books I read when I was getting back into reading, and for years it has sat on my shelves with a four-star rating, allowing me to justify my relationship with Kasie West as “complicated” whenever is suited my easily charmed fancy.<br /><br />But no longer!<br /><br /><br />Because I reread it and...actually did like it?<br /><br />On the Fence is not a game changer, or anything. It did not change my life, or my View Of the World. I did not love it, or even reallyyy like it.<br /><br />I precisely liked it. <br /><br />There’s a lot of not like other girls stuff at the beginning (and also girl hate because my suffering on this planet will never end), but surprisingly, it’s mostly resolved by character development. The Big Theme (a requirement of every contemporary) is that girls don’t have to fit in with the idea of the traditionally feminine, but also they can if they want to and that’s chill too.<br /><br />Which, if you’ve read other Kasie West books, may surprise you. But a pleasant surprise!<br /><br />That theme was pretty sloppily done, and also never even once extends to guys (who either exist outside of gender roles, like super-society heroes, or live so deeply within them that escape is not a remote possibility - hard to say). But I was just so astonished that our protagonist wasn’t consistently not like other girls’d to the last page that I kind of...enjoyed this.<br /><br />Bottom line: Fine! (This has been the closest to a rave review of a Kasie West book you will ever see from me.)<br /><br />----------- <br /><br />the fact that this was a million jillion times better than any other Kasie West book, like not-even-by-the-same-author-what-the-hell-major-improvement levels of disparity, and it's a 3.5 star rating says everything you need to know about my relationship with Kasie West.<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />----------- <br /><br />it is my duty as a responsible citizen to periodically reread contemporaries i once liked in order to make sure i still like them. some may call me a hero.......and yeah i'd have to agree</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6740156874657831363">I’m absolutely terrified about writing a review to this book. All I know is that the writer should never write a sequel to this book, especially one set a decade into the future. It’s a sweet love story that might mean that the protagonists in all likelihood peaked out early in life.<br/><br/>The words went by quickly. These emotions that are in my mind are bittersweet to me. To tell the truth, people like Braden and Charlie seem like a kaleidoscopic couple who don’t exist in my country. Do they exist in </span>
  <span id="freeText6740156874657831363" style="display:none">I’m absolutely terrified about writing a review to this book. All I know is that the writer should never write a sequel to this book, especially one set a decade into the future. It’s a sweet love story that might mean that the protagonists in all likelihood peaked out early in life.<br /><br />The words went by quickly. These emotions that are in my mind are bittersweet to me. To tell the truth, people like Braden and Charlie seem like a kaleidoscopic couple who don’t exist in my country. Do they exist in the US? Probably. Do all teens who read this book turn out kind and honest? Hell no.<br /><br />That's why it’s my pet theory that people who become unromantic, jaded, bitter, mean, and cruel in life have been harmed, denied, starved of love, and conditioned. As for me, I am grateful for the air that I breathe, the lungs that do their work, the blood cells that carry the oxygen and allow me to live. You have two lives in this world, and the second one begins when you realize you have only one life.</span>

<div id="review_1037663191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1037663191" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1037663191?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=cute">cute</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=sports">sports</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1037663191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15966407932354027407">Charlie is a sixteen-year-old teen who likes playing sports, especially soccer, watching sport games and hanging out with her <strong><em>three</em> </strong>brothers. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409123228i/10936989.jpg' alt='description' width='330' height='220' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She’s not your typical teenage girl since she prefers watching a soccer game (or playing it) than go shopping or reading or going to the cinema, etc.<br/><br/>That’s why she and I couldn't quite ever be best friends but she’s a nice girl so, sure, we could at least get along. But, see, I’m the kind of the girl who will exclusively cheer for players and not be one my</span>
  <span id="freeText15966407932354027407" style="display:none">Charlie is a sixteen-year-old teen who likes playing sports, especially soccer, watching sport games and hanging out with her <strong><em>three</em> </strong>brothers. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409123228i/10936989.jpg" alt="description" width="330" height="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She’s not your typical teenage girl since she prefers watching a soccer game (or playing it) than go shopping or reading or going to the cinema, etc.<br><br>That’s why she and I couldn't quite ever be best friends but she’s a nice girl so, sure, we could at least get along. But, see, I’m the kind of the girl who will exclusively cheer for players and not be one myself, except if we’re talking about badminton, dancing, cheerleading or gymnastics (which aren’t in Charlie’s list of sports to practice.)<br><br>The point is that I couldn’t very much connect with her and…why is she wearing a <em>dress </em>on the cover? Yes, she has a bit of a character development and yes she does get more feminine but, the way I see it, that pretty little summer dress doesn’t match her personality so when I look at that cover it doesn't feel like it's Charlie that I see with the guy.<br><br><strong>While I think this was a clichéd story</strong> (I mean come on…you fall in love with your neighbour who you’ve known since being a child and it takes you to date another guy to see it? Yup, not impressed) <strong>and a quite unrealistic one,</strong> (who actually has that of a good relationship with their three brothers + father + gets a job without even wanting one?)<strong> it was also fast-paced, fun and I certainly had a good time reading it.</strong><br><br>The romance was light and cute, absolutely typical of contemporary YA. Nonetheless, that didn’t keep me from thinking it was good and lovely. Braden wasn’t actually my favorite guy, even though he and Charlie get along very well and have much in common. I prefer Evan all the way. That’s when I concluded that she and I are quite different. Is that a bad thing? Absolutely not. But in order to <strong>
  <em>love</em>
</strong> a certain book, I like feeling some connecting to a main character and feel common interest.<br><br>I was lying, actually, when I truly thought she and I were not alike was when <strong>she said in the story that she doesn’t know who wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a>.</strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409123228ra/10936990.gif" alt="description" width="450" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Exactly! I couldn’t believe my eyes! Maybe you would thing that it's okay (I’m not saying it's necessarily a bad thing) but that really killed the small connection I had with her because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1885.Pride_and_Prejudice" title="Pride and Prejudice by Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener">Pride and Prejudice</a> is my favorite classic (and I’m in love with Mr. Darcy—who isn’t? *winks*)<br><br>The writing was good and, in general, the story was interesting. Plus, even though the characters felt clichéd, I liked how the story went. It may have been predictable but there were always small things happening that made that fact not an obvious problem.<br><br>I would recommend this to anyone seeking a light contemporary read perfect for summer (especially if you’re a fan of sports and characters similar to Charlie.)<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15966407932354027407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText12950735152047380212" style="display:none">out of all of kasie wests books, i for sure thought this was going to be the one to steal my heart. i mean, the whole 'falling for the boy next door' is my absolute favourite trope of all time. i adore stories about childhood friends/neighbours becoming more. so it makes me sad that this particular story didnt sweep me off my feet.<br /><br />i mean, its entertaining and it has the ending that i was rooting for, but there is something very shallow about this novel. its explores a lot of great coming-of-age and first romance themes, but they dont seem to be well-developed. its superficial, at best. not sure how to explain it. its light and cute, but i just wanted <i>more</i> from it. especially when it came to the relationship between charlie and braden. oh well.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1219630334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219630334" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219630334?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219630334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11680540755261357705"><br/>I don’t remember the underlying deeper themes in the novel. All I remember when I read it then was the fluff and it being a summer breezy read. I didn't realize Skye from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15283043.The_Distance_Between_Us' title='The Distance Between Us by Kasie West' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Distance Between Us</a> is a character here and Caymen is mentioned at least once because their shops are practically beside Charlie's workplace. I couldn’t even remember the things <b>Braden</b> and <b>Charlie</b> talked about and how it started with them trying to prove which one knows the other better. Clearly their feelings for each othe</span>
  <span id="freeText11680540755261357705" style="display:none"><br>I don’t remember the underlying deeper themes in the novel. All I remember when I read it then was the fluff and it being a summer breezy read. I didn't realize Skye from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15283043.The_Distance_Between_Us" title="The Distance Between Us by Kasie West" rel="nofollow noopener">The Distance Between Us</a> is a character here and Caymen is mentioned at least once because their shops are practically beside Charlie's workplace. I couldn’t even remember the things <b>Braden</b> and <b>Charlie</b> talked about and how it started with them trying to prove which one knows the other better. Clearly their feelings for each other have been building up since they were practically children so them being together in the end didn’t come from nowhere. I was so wrong. Did I not know how to read three years ago? Jeez!<br>_ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ _ <br><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW WRITTEN MARCH 2015 </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381197348ra/4502962.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>(I’d love for Chloe Moretz to play Charlie’s role in case this gets optioned for a movie.)<br><br>This is exactly what I needed- a cuddly, snuggly book to read and it gave me this overall warm and pleasant feeling. <br> <br>This is a sunshiny story about a tomboy, Charlie (short for Charlotte) and her way to one of the most difficult endeavors in her life that is to figure out who she is and who she wants to be despite being the only girl in the family. <br><br>Charlie is a very easy-to-relate-to character as I believe every girl went through/will go through that “tomboy” stage. Well maybe not every girl, but I sure did which is a bit peculiar in my case because I have four sisters who are all epitomes of what a proper woman should be. Why I decided to follow my only brother’s or my dad’s path for that matter back then, I ‘m not really sure. (<i> In high school, I used to wear my dad’s oversized jackets with matching baggy pants to school and thought I was so cool. How dreadful! Lol. </i>)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426040078i/13966488._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But anyways, back to the story, a far worse challenge Charlie somehow finds herself struggling with is her feelings for her and her family’s best friend- Braden who apparently has only sisterly feelings for her. <br><br><i> <b> “This was the definition of torture- loving someone who only wanted to be your friend. “ </b></i><br><br>There is this scene in the middle of the book where I just felt this strong sympathy for Charlie. It’s amazing how the author seems to know exactly how it feels to dodge/sugarcoat your true reaction to an obvious rejection. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426040078ra/13966489.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I love the flow and transitions of the events in the story via the use of simple and heartfelt writing you can easily go along with. It becomes all the more appealing and entertaining especially since the story is told in Charlie’s POV. <br><br> <b> <i> “My heart thought that was the time to beat out of control.” </i> </b><br><br> I especially enjoyed how she blames every unfortunate event that happens in her life to make up. Lol. I also like the use of short chapters and the summer setting that make the story very light and easy to read. <br><br>The major thing that quite put me off however is the sudden overturn of events towards the end especially between Braden and Charlie. I was like “woah!!!“<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1387847461ra/7680796.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I even had to go back a few pages to check if I missed some parts, but I didn’t. A slower, more elaborate process would have been much more believable but overall, this was a generally enjoyable read and it has a giddily happy ending via an end of summer party (Cliché-ish? Well most happy endings are.^^)</span>
  <a data-text-id="11680540755261357705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16794710661764526609">Okay... can’t say I got much sleep last night/early this morning, because this beauty didn’t let me😅 I can easily say this book was so worth my sleep deprivation. <br/>This story was beautiful, funny, heartwarming, soo sad, relatable, addicting and a really easy read. <br/><br/>Charlie reminded me so much of my little sister it was astonishing!   <span id="freeText16794710661764526609" style="display:none">Okay... can’t say I got much sleep last night/early this morning, because this beauty didn’t let me😅 I can easily say this book was so worth my sleep deprivation. <br />This story was beautiful, funny, heartwarming, soo sad, relatable, addicting and a really easy read. <br /><br />Charlie reminded me so much of my little sister it was astonishing! She could beat all the guys in almost everything, she was hilarious, didn’t have any girl friends who didn’t play sports and was so strong emotionally it was amazing! <br />Her having 3 (not counting her Best Friend Braden who was like a brother to her, until a few years ago) tall, athletic and protective brothers was really relatable because they reminded me of my five brothers, lol. <br /><br />I loved all the characters in here, like really all. Braden, Jerom, Nathan, and Gage were my main favorites, though, supportive, protective, hilarious, athletic, and caring they were the best friends and brothers any sister and/or girl could ask for. <br /><br />The mention of the band Crusty Toads with the same band members in the story was completely epic! <br /><br />Loved this one to the moon and back🖤<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_743343875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743343875" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743343875?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=next-door">next-door</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=laugh-aloud">laugh-aloud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=rereading-material">rereading-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=beloved">beloved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=great-books">great-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=best-of">best-of</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743343875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17447550930305749690">That's it, I found a book I want to live in.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/early-review-on-the-fence.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392025710i/8489283.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>For me this book was perfect: perfectly-awesome dynamics, perfectly-sweet romance and just a perfectly-bit of sadness to make up for the perfectly-amazing ‘giggleness’.<br/>Yes, I am a also a ‘perfect’ dork in love with romantic stories, but what can I say? I just loved this story so very much!<br/><br/>And you shouldn’t simply take my words for it, so I will give you the reasons why those items on the list were so great to begin with:<br/>1. fantastic family dynamics</span>
  <span id="freeText17447550930305749690" style="display:none">That's it, I found a book I want to live in.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/early-review-on-the-fence.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392025710i/8489283.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For me this book was perfect: perfectly-awesome dynamics, perfectly-sweet romance and just a perfectly-bit of sadness to make up for the perfectly-amazing ‘giggleness’.<br>Yes, I am a also a ‘perfect’ dork in love with romantic stories, but what can I say? I just loved this story so very much!<br><br>And you shouldn’t simply take my words for it, so I will give you the reasons why those items on the list were so great to begin with:<br>1. fantastic family dynamics - from honest punishments, to love, teasing, comforting, helping.. everything was relatable, realistic and just as beautiful as any family should be.<br>2. best friendships – they are all so great together as friends, having fun, playing sports or just being themselves and nothing more.<br>3. cutest love story – I simply loved the fence scenes – their game was cute and honest :D and there were sparks, and beauty and so much fun.<br><br>Not to mention that:<br>- I had FUN! Tons of it!<br>- I laughed out loud. I giggled like a kid. I smiled until my face hurt.<br>- I highlighted half the book (it involved funny moments, and teasing, and some meaningful words and pretty much a lot of awesomeness). It was this great and more!<br><br>The romance is slow.. And sweet.. And it has that confusing vibe that only first loves (teenage loves) can ever give. It also happened during the entire story and it was based on friendship and trust and history – all ingredients for a great realistic and fun romance.<br><br>There is talk at some point about ‘love’ which might seem a bit too early (even though it happens near the end of the story), but it felt somehow right when I thought of it – because she loved him as a brother, as a neighbor, and afterwards she realised that her feelings were about more than just that – she loved him as a guy too.<br>The transition was sweet, with her discovering all the different ways she might get to act around him – noticing new things about him, blushing at times, actually making a completely fool of herself too.. And it’s true, I wanted the author to take the time and put an “I love you” line in the first pages just to enforce what I am saying here – that there was ‘love’ first in their friendship, but it worked nicely anyways. It’s just a statement, not a problem at all.<br><br>Also, there is a bit of drama, no wonder the comparison I made way up there, but it’s not gut wrenching – it’s in there more for the character’s sake than for ours. It shows how strong she becomes, how vulnerable she might be deep down, it shows how much love there is between the characters, it’s a missing piece in Charlie’s life that she needs to find in order to be complete again.<br><br>After all, “On the Fence” is a self-discovery kind of story.<br>Charlie lived in this bubble created by ‘the safeness of brotherhood’ (my words) and she knows that there is more to her, so she makes new (girl) friends, she goes out to meet new people, she takes a job and in time becomes more responsible (or at least she finds out that even small actions can have consequences).<br><br>CONCLUSION:<br><br>One of the very best romantic stories out there. <br>Keep an eye on it when it comes out this summer!<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/early-review-on-the-fence.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>*Find this and more at: <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/kasie-west/early-review-on-the-fence.html" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a><br>** ARC received from the publisher for review. Thank you!<br><br>___________________________________________<br><br>Pre-reading:<br>While waiting like crazy for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712140013" rel="nofollow noopener">'Split Second'</a> I will enjoy this beauty here. Oh well.. Seems like a fair trade :D<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1391865828i/8467999.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1911021650" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1911021650?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=contemperary">contemperary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1911021650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14804919221913401570">Upon reread: still five stars. Still obcessed. These are some of my favorite characters - I just want to live in this book. It also contains several of my favorite romance tropes<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ boy next door, friends to lovers, nice guy as the love interest  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><br/>This is my new obsession. I'm so sad that it's over. I'll be thinking about this book for a long long time. And I'm sure I'll be rereading it soon too.<br/><br/>I was fifty pages in, still didn't know who the romantic interest would be </span>
  <span id="freeText14804919221913401570" style="display:none">Upon reread: still five stars. Still obcessed. These are some of my favorite characters - I just want to live in this book. It also contains several of my favorite romance tropes<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ boy next door, friends to lovers, nice guy as the love interest  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />This is my new obsession. I'm so sad that it's over. I'll be thinking about this book for a long long time. And I'm sure I'll be rereading it soon too.<br /><br />I was fifty pages in, still didn't know who the romantic interest would be (though I had guessed) and already I knew it was going to be one of my new favorite books. Kasie West did such an incredible job at building real, interesting, deep characters and all I wanted was to live in this world. I wanted so badly to be friends with these people. <br /><br />The romance was cute, but it was a slow burn and didn't even take the main focus of the story. It was much deeper than that about family, friendship, figuring out who you are, and learning how to be honest about who you want to be. This book was so satisfying and I'll be talking about it for a very long time.</span>

<div id="review_703963417" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/703963417" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/703963417?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=swoony-guys">swoony-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=writing-envy">writing-envy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=omg-the-cover-people">omg-the-cover-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=2014-favourites">2014-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer703963417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6738837051951994561">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>4.5 stars<br/><br/>PROPER REVIEW. FANGIRLING AND INITIAL REACTIONS IS BELOW.</b><br/><br/>It has been almost half a year since I picked up On The Fence and fell in love with it. During this span of time I have reread it 3 times; recommended this author to my friends multiple times and have thought about this book more than I'd like to admit. In my experience, no one has written better cute and fluffy reads than Kasie West. This woman knows exactly how to catch our hearts, pull the r</span>
  <span id="freeText6738837051951994561" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br><br><b>4.5 stars<br><br>PROPER REVIEW. FANGIRLING AND INITIAL REACTIONS IS BELOW.</b><br><br>It has been almost half a year since I picked up On The Fence and fell in love with it. During this span of time I have reread it 3 times; recommended this author to my friends multiple times and have thought about this book more than I'd like to admit. In my experience, no one has written better cute and fluffy reads than Kasie West. This woman knows exactly how to catch our hearts, pull the right strings and hits all the right notes. On The Fence was exactly that, and if not transcended my uber high expectations even more.<br><br>Charlotte (Charlie) is a tomboy. Ever since her mother died when she was six, Charlie has been the only female in her family. She's got three older brothers and a father as well as a tight friendship with her next door neighbour, Braden. I absolutely loved Charlie and her tough and hard-centred core. She knows how to deal with boys and loves her sports. She's never worn makeup in her life and plans to keep it that way. She doesn't give a crap about what others think of her and she was an incredibly enjoyable protagonist to follow. I sometimes was shaken off course by her abrupt coldness--such as that time when one of her teammate's grandmother died and Charlie wasn't the slightest bit sincere--but we soon find out that there was something behind those types of actions.<br><br>The highlight of Kasie West's latest is the relationships she created. I LOVED the relationship Charlie held with her brothers. They treat her as an equal and include her in everything. It was incredibly entertaining to watch them bicker and they're always looking out for one and another. One of the best sibling relationships I've seen so far this year.<br><br>The romance in one word? OMFGIAMINLOVE (that is one word don't you dare question it). Charlie and Braden's romance is a slow burn one and I shipped them from page one. Braden is really close with Charlie's family as Braden has quite a few problems with his family at home, it was really nice to see them as friends first then watch them realise their feelings for each other. Everything about their relationship was shippable. And the fence chats *sighs*<br><br>Personally, I would have liked to know more about Charlie's time at her soccer camp. I understand that it wasn't a huge focal point but I found the camp to be really interesting and I wanted to know more about it, especially since Charlie talked quite a number of times. Qualm aside, On The Fence kept a smile painted on my face the entire time. Definitely not one to miss, Kasie West once again offers a sweet romance, amazing sibling relationship and totally unforced humour.<br><p>
  <em>~Thank you HarperCollins Australia for sending me this copy!~</em>
</p><br><br>---------<br><br>IT HAPPENED. <br><br>Finished at 12:39am last night. I didn't sleep until 1:15am because I couldn't stop squealing. <br><br>This was me throughout the entire book: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380850962ra/3134920.gif" width="500" height="270" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I COULD NOT TAKE THE SMILE OFF MY FACE. <br><br>My life is now complete.<br><br><img alt="" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/680221.gif" width="500" height="277" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>************<br><br>IT'S HAPPENING. <br><br>SQUEEEEEEEEEEEEE</span>

<div id="review_950683479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/950683479" />
    <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired"><img alt="Rashika (is tired)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476647072p2/8492956.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/950683479?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rashika (is tired)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rashika (is tired)" href="/user/show/8492956-rashika-is-tired">Rashika (is tired)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=everyone-loved-but-me">everyone-loved-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=meh-romance">meh-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=good-secondary-characters">good-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=e-arcs">e-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=wimpy-or-i-no-like-mcs">wimpy-or-i-no-like-mcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8492956-rashika-is-tired?shelf=realistic-contemporary">realistic-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer950683479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1891258744926770567">I am a party-pooper. Although a sad one since I am somewhat sad I didn’t enjoy this. There is quite a bit of hype surrounding this book and all my friends who have read it so far have loved it so I feel like a complete buzz kill with my ‘hating’. <br/><br/><i>On the Fence</i>, quite frankly, sucked. I went in expecting a friends-to-more romance and got something else. <br/><br/>For starters, I did NOT like the main character. I was cringing the whole time I was reading this book and was not the least bit amused. I think w</span>
  <span id="freeText1891258744926770567" style="display:none">I am a party-pooper. Although a sad one since I am somewhat sad I didn’t enjoy this. There is quite a bit of hype surrounding this book and all my friends who have read it so far have loved it so I feel like a complete buzz kill with my ‘hating’. <br /><br /><i>On the Fence</i>, quite frankly, sucked. I went in expecting a friends-to-more romance and got something else. <br /><br />For starters, I did NOT like the main character. I was cringing the whole time I was reading this book and was not the least bit amused. I think what bothered me the most was this whole normal girl vs not normal girl thing going on. I get that teenagers go through a phase where they aren’t sure of themselves, I went through it too but the whole changing yourself to fit in storylines have never worked for me. Perhaps it’s my fault but if I had known this book had a storyline that revolved around the character trying to change herself, I probably wouldn’t have read it. <br /><br />My problem with this whole thing is that it seems to say that there is a ‘right’ way to be a female but there isn’t! Femininity isn’t defined by whether you are girly or not! I am neither girly nor a tom boy but I am no less female then other girls out there. I think what made this worse was that Charlie seemed to be the only ‘tom boy’ in this book. She was surrounded by girly girls who only seemed to care about make-up. The stereotypes started getting to me and I ended up being so annoyed. Plus I never understood why Charlie felt this need to hide things from her family. Why was she so embarrassed if that’s what she wanted to be? Didn't she understand that her family would love her no matter what? I mean seeing that she is such a 'family' person... I kind of expected more from her.<br /><br />It didn’t end there though. The romance bothered the living daylights out of me. WHERE WAS THE SWOON I WAS PROMISED? Braden and Charlie’s romance is basically non-existent. It seems like one moment she thinks of him as a brother and the next he isn’t a brother to her. Did she have a crush on him before the book started? I have no idea because it was never said (or I missed it). <br /><br />When the ‘other’ dude is brought into the picture things become even more awkward with Charlie sticking her head in the sand. She doesn't see that there is a reason why Braden does NOT like the dude while her brothers don’t mind him nearly as much. I never actually sensed sparks between them and while they didn’t lack chemistry, things seemed too rushed in the end. The L word popped out of nowhere. And I do say nowhere. Just because they have known each other forever doesn’t mean that they can pop out the L word and it won’t seem random. <br /><br />The only redeeming factor for me is Charlie’s family. Her dad is a sweet heart and I cannot imagine how hard things must be for him. Her brothers are also incredible and so fun to read about!<br /><br />I guess one could also fault the length of the book in this case because it did seem quite short in the end. It’s not a short book by any means but it did seem a little rushed. Things started getting good about 80% into the novel but just as I was starting to like it, I was drowned in a bucket of cheese and that ultimately killed the book for me. I only felt relief when I finished this book. <br /><br />With all that said though, I do want to read <i>The Distance Between Us</i> because I think it might be more enjoyable for me as a reader and if not that, <i>Pivot Point</i>. I am not ready to give up on the author yet. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1891258744926770567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1442643332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1442643332" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1442643332?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442643332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5494282134058410687"><a href='https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Fafa's Book Corner (Wordpress) </a><br/><a href='http://fafasbookcorner.blogspot.ca/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Fafa's Book Corner (Blogger) </a><br/><br/>Beware spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>This book was recommended to me by my GR friend <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698957324' rel='nofollow noopener'> Alyssa </a>! Click on her name to read her review.<br/><br/>I had originally added this book back in February. I was going through a chick lit phase and thought that all of Kasie West's books would be excellent additions. But because I thought they would turn out to be shallow I took them all off. It wasn't until I stumbled upon Alyssa's review that I decided to read all her boo</span>
  <span id="freeText5494282134058410687" style="display:none"><a href="https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fafa's Book Corner (Wordpress) </a><br /><a href="http://fafasbookcorner.blogspot.ca/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fafa's Book Corner (Blogger) </a><br /><br />Beware spoilers ahead!<br /><br />This book was recommended to me by my GR friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/698957324" rel="nofollow noopener"> Alyssa </a>! Click on her name to read her review.<br /><br />I had originally added this book back in February. I was going through a chick lit phase and thought that all of Kasie West's books would be excellent additions. But because I thought they would turn out to be shallow I took them all off. It wasn't until I stumbled upon Alyssa's review that I decided to read all her books. I am happy to say that I enjoyed this!<br /><br />As is with all of Kasie West's books, this book is written in first person in Charlie's point of view.<br /><br />The book begins with Charlie as she is pulled over by a police officer for breaking the speed limit. Charlie is about to use the fact that her father is a cop, but then the cop mentions that this is not his first time pulling her over. She accepts her ticket. When she gets home her brothers and Braden are having another bet. If a person does not drink the weird smoothie that Gage made then they have to dump it on themselves.<br /><br />Charlie getting rattled by Braden drinks it. Her brothers and and Braden now have to dump the smoothie on themselves. On Charlie's command they all set off for a run.<br /><br />A few days after this Charlie's father confronts her on the ticket she got. She didn't tell him and he was not happy to here it from one of his coworkers. He tells Charlie that she has to get a job to earn the money for the tickets. Charlie tries to protest as does her brother, but their father does not budge.<br /><br />Her brother Gage offers to help Charlie look for a job. Upon looking a majority of what Gage does is flirt with girls. They come across a shop and the girl Skye tells Charlie that there is a shop that is hiring. And to tell the shop owner that Skye sent her over. <br /><br />When Charlie finds the shop it is not what she excepts. It's a Bazaar that sells clothes that Charlie does not wear. And the owner Linda is very odd. Desperate Charlie takes the position making a vow to quit after her tickets have been paid. Linda tells Charlie that she will have to buy some more fashion forward clothes. She suggests that on Charlie's first day she will pick out some clothes for her and fill out the paper work.<br /><br />Once she gets her job she finds it hard to sleep at night and this is because she isn't running anymore. When she runs she falls asleep quickly and this keeps the nightmares at bay. When Charlie was 6 years old her mother got into a car accident. She has nightmares of said car accident.<br /><br />Seeing as she can't sleep she decides to have a conversation with Braden. A fence chat. They play this game to see who knows more about the other. Which makes Charlie happy and helps her forget what kept her up.<br /><br />Braden seems to benefit from these conversations as well. His father verbally abuses his mother and him whenever he is drunk. He suffered a back injury a few years ago and since then has developed an addiction. <br /><br />To be honest I did not except to fall in love with this book. In the beginning Charlie was annoying. All she cared about were sports and winning. She was cold and did not care for others emotions. But as I read on she became likable and in ways relatable. <br /><br />There are cameos from The Distance Between Us. Skye comes in frequently and it was nice to read about her and Charlie's friendship. Charlie and her families relationship was sweet. Her brothers were very protective of her as was her father. <br /><br />The fence chats between Charlie and Braden were sweet. Charlie found it much easier to talk to the fence then she did to Braden's face. I liked reading about their game and learning more about them. The romance in this book was slow burn. It was pretty awkward considering that Braden is Charlie's brother's best friend.<br /><br />It was sweet how supportive Braden was with Charlie. Even when she did test his patience. As a character Braden was nice but I didn't like him. And in turn I couldn't really see the romance between the two of them. They felt like best friends to me and that's it. <br /><br />Linda was absolutely weird in the beginning of the book but she grew on me as well as Charlie. She turned out to be a mother figure towards Charlie and Skye. During her job Charlie meets this girl Amber and the two become friends. Unlike Charlie's other friends she is girly and does not like sports. I was happy that Charlie didn't judge Amber for that. Their friendship was sweet!<br /><br />The best part of this book was Charlie's character. I liked how she didn't instantly hate all girly girls, and how when she turned 16 (the dating age her brothers set) she didn't instantly want to date guys. Charlie is pretty tough and throughout this book she goes through a self-discovery journey. She finds that she does not hate the clothes Linda chose for her, she doesn't even mind make-up, and she likes her job.<br /><br />During this book Charlie starts to become self-conscious about what others think about her. She had two different lives. The Charlie who loved sports and the Charlie who dressed up for work. For most of the book she doesn't tell her brothers about the clothes Linda bought or how she started modeling for make-up. She thinks that her brothers would only make fun of her. And with Amber she thought that Amber wouldn't like the side of her that played sports. She even pretended not to know anything about sports when she started dating this guy Evan. She thought he only wanted a girl who cheered him on not a girl who could play against him. Eventually she accepts these sides of herself and stops hiding it from people.<br /><br />The most important thing that was brought up in this book was how society or people in our lives start categorizing us in these bubbles. In Charlie brother's point of view she could not like make-up and wear pretty clothes. So when it came out that she did they treated her like an alien. They have even said that Charlie isn't a normal girl. There is no such thing as a normal girl or boy. Everyone is unique and different. And as people we could become whoever we want to be. I loved how the author incorporated this!<br /><br />Overall this was a fantastic book! I would recommend this to everyone because there is something in here that we can all relate to.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5494282134058410687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1886173128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7104495671275595610">About: On the Fence is a young adult fiction written by Kasie West. It was published on 7/1/14 by HarperTeen, an imprint of HarperCollins, 304 pages. The genres are young adult, fiction, contemporary, and romance.<br/><br/>My Experience: I started reading On the Fence on 6/13/17 and finished it on 6/19/17. This book is a fantastic read! I love the humor and the family dynamic! I love Charlie’s three brothers and how protective they are of her. I love the easy going between the siblings. I like the differe</span>
  <span id="freeText7104495671275595610" style="display:none">About: On the Fence is a young adult fiction written by Kasie West. It was published on 7/1/14 by HarperTeen, an imprint of HarperCollins, 304 pages. The genres are young adult, fiction, contemporary, and romance.<br /><br />My Experience: I started reading On the Fence on 6/13/17 and finished it on 6/19/17. This book is a fantastic read! I love the humor and the family dynamic! I love Charlie’s three brothers and how protective they are of her. I love the easy going between the siblings. I like the different personalities of each characters and Gage is actually my favorite.<br /><br />“Hey, guys. Don’t be idiots. This is Evan. Evan, the angry-looking one is Jerom, the constipated-looking one is Nathan, and the goofball on the right is Gage.” p198<br /><br />In this book, readers will follow the point of view of Charlotte (Charlie) Reynolds, sixteen, the only girl in the family with 3 older brothers Jerom, Nathan, and Gage, and a police officer for a father. Their best friend is Braden Lewis, the neighbor next door. It’s no surprise that Charlie is a tomboy who likes sports. She plays football, soccer, and basketball with her brothers and Braden. She’s part of the guys, including getting speeding tickets. Her dad is fed up with paying her speeding tickets for her and challenged her to get a job. Working at a boutique requires her to wear feminine clothing and her wardrobe is anything but. Through this job, she learns to embrace the girly side of herself that was not part of her growing up, including wearing makeup and hanging out with girls who don’t play sports. Charlie feels broken due to a many reasons and often has trouble sleeping. She turns to the fence in her backyard for comfort. From there, her feelings begins to surface but she worries the feelings is one sided.<br /><br />“By a show of hands, who here would’ve asked Charlie out in the last six months had they not been given the ‘We will kill you if you look at Charlie’ speech by the three lugs over there when she turned sixteen?” p201<br /><br />I couldn’t put down this book! I like Charlie’s dad’s new co-worker Carol. That’s a very unique idea. I like the fence chat concept, although, I wonder how they survive on so little sleep. I like their tips on which guy or girls to not date. The humor is contagious in this book and I couldn’t help but laugh out loud. I like that Charlie is open minded and a team player because even though she doesn’t care for extreme girly displays on her clothes, she still wears the bedazzled jersey Amber made for her. I highly recommend you all to read this book!<br /><br />Pro: humor, family dynamic, friendship, page turner, fast paced, easy to read<br /><br />Con: none<br /><br />I rate it 5 stars!<br /><br />***Disclaimer: I borrowed this book from my local public library and my opinions are honest.<br /><br />xoxo,<br /> Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for a detailed review<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7104495671275595610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer758492974" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4423010319640402693">Kasie West is the reason why I don't write off contemporary straight out of my to-be-read list. It's because she writes such cute stories with a lot of characters who are always set on doing the right thing.<br/><br/>Charlie is the easily relatable character that I understood. Sure she hardly had any self-esteem, but when you're a teenager, you certainly don't know any better. Honestly if there was no back and fourth, the book would probably get super boring. Self-deprecating characters aren't always the </span>
  <span id="freeText4423010319640402693" style="display:none">Kasie West is the reason why I don't write off contemporary straight out of my to-be-read list. It's because she writes such cute stories with a lot of characters who are always set on doing the right thing.<br /><br />Charlie is the easily relatable character that I understood. Sure she hardly had any self-esteem, but when you're a teenager, you certainly don't know any better. Honestly if there was no back and fourth, the book would probably get super boring. Self-deprecating characters aren't always the easiest to read about, but if you were a little like her character when you're younger, you can remember what it was like. Also dating someone you're not into wasn't exactly the best decision. That's why you have these years to iron out the kinks. I loved how annoying her brothers were too. And her father was super sweet.<br /><br />I love stories where a friendship blossoms into something more and this is definitely one of them. Kasie West reminds me a lot of Miranda Kenneally's books and I just love them both. If you're looking for a cute contemporary romance, pick this one up. I'm not usually a big contemporary fan, but her writing is too cute to pass up.<br /><br />RATING 4/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />"I didn't feel like I had a purpose, a goal. But after a while I let my long relax and realized not everything had to have a point. Some things could just be the for the fun of it." (149)<br /><br />"I am going to call every girl in your contacts tonight and tell them you're gay." (168)<br /><br />"It's pretty impressive that a girl that looks like you knows so much about baseball." (189)<br /><br />"If you can't be yourself around him, then you shouldn't be dating him." (193)<br /><br />"Guys don't want a competitor, they want a cheerleader." (194)<br /><br />"We can't let boys define how we feel about ourselves. You have to know who you are before you should let any boy worth anything in." (211)<br /><br />"If he doesn't want you for you, then he's not worth it." (228)</span>

<div id="review_1315350657" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1315350657" />
    <a title="Anja H." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h"><img alt="Anja H." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559051853p2/6054186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1315350657?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anja H." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anja H." href="/user/show/6054186-anja-h">Anja H.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315350657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9853610199888269576"><b>*4.5 TOMBOYISH STARS*</b><br/><br/><i>
  <b>"Sometimes we expect more than people are capable of giving at the moment."</b>
</i><br/><br/>When I first started this, I thought I wasn't going to like this one. I changed my mind pretty quickly though, because I totally love it now!<br/>This novel is about Charlotte/Charlie, who is a total tomboy who grew up with 3 brothers and no mother, only a father. She's really close with her neighbor Braden, who's more like her 4th brother. Then she gets a job at a clothing store and discovers the girl</span>
  <span id="freeText9853610199888269576" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 TOMBOYISH STARS*</b><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"Sometimes we expect more than people are capable of giving at the moment."</b>
</i><br /><br />When I first started this, I thought I wasn't going to like this one. I changed my mind pretty quickly though, because I totally love it now!<br />This novel is about Charlotte/Charlie, who is a total tomboy who grew up with 3 brothers and no mother, only a father. She's really close with her neighbor Braden, who's more like her 4th brother. Then she gets a job at a clothing store and discovers the girly side of life and her newfound feelings for Braden while simultaneously trying to get over her mother's death and her nightmares.<br /><br />I really loved Charlie's character development! At first I really didn't like her, but eventually she changed from a closed-off and pretty selfish girl to a more openminded and happier woman in the end. <br />I almost immediately shipped her with Braden, I saw right away that those two were perfect for each other! That doesn't mean that I didn't like Evan, but I'm glad she didn't end up with him anyway.<br />Charlie made a lot of new friends on the way, like Amber, Skye and Linda. What I also liked was her close relationship with her father and brothers. I can't even imagine what it must be like to grow up without a woman in my life to help me through all the tough times. It makes me respect single fathers so much more!<br />The ending of the book was also totally perfect, with that last fence reference. I really liked the book title, as the fence played a key part in Charlie's journey and her relationship with Braden.<br /><br />Overall, I really liked the book. It wasn't perfect, obviously, but not many books are! It was definitely a cute, feel-good story, but don't expect anything too deep! I still have yet to encounter a Kasie West book that I didn't like. I guess I'm going to have to read the <i>Pivot Point</i> series real soon.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9853610199888269576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1224243141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7039863147658615350">As I've said,I'm going to read more of Kasie West's novels and this is just the perfect day to read my 2nd book of Kasie,as I am reminded of my friend's birthday today. According to my sister,this friend of ours is a fan of this author(thanks to you,Aj!) So,NEIL my awesome buddy,HAPPY,HAPPY BIRTHDAY TO YOU!^^<br/><br/>My Review:<br/>Now,I understand why this buddy of mine love Kasie West..it's because this author has a thing in creating her characters.And in this novel,it is the awesome characters that made me</span>
  <span id="freeText7039863147658615350" style="display:none">As I've said,I'm going to read more of Kasie West's novels and this is just the perfect day to read my 2nd book of Kasie,as I am reminded of my friend's birthday today. According to my sister,this friend of ours is a fan of this author(thanks to you,Aj!) So,NEIL my awesome buddy,HAPPY,HAPPY BIRTHDAY TO YOU!^^<br /><br />My Review:<br />Now,I understand why this buddy of mine love Kasie West..it's because this author has a thing in creating her characters.And in this novel,it is the awesome characters that made me love this book.<br /><br />Let me start with the MC..CHARLIE(Charlotte),a 16 year old tough,rough,smart,witty and beautiful young lady,grew up with her dad and three brothers plus,the boy neighbor who they considered family.Living with these boys all her life explains very well why she's a tomboy..she doesn't wear make up,never wear skirts,and doesn't care how and what she look..Until one day,when for the first time,she had to work in a boutique to pay off a speeding ticket and(bam!)was introduced to a world of fashion and make up.<br /><br />Charlie,since childhood only hangs out with boys(her brothers,their friends,and Braden-the 4th brother). She plays with them,watch baseball games with them,and do whatever the boys want..just to have fun.And I just loved this part because it made me remember my childhood memories as well,with my four amazing and lovely sisters and my only handsome brother(my twin brother).<br /><br />I loved all the relationships here: from Charlies relationship with her brothers,friends,her dad..Oh yes,her dad! I adored her dad so much! Her dad's so sweet,and over protective!(just like my dad). He even got himself a book on "How to Raise a Teenage Girl"!how responsible,right? And of course,her relationship with Braden(which are for you,my co-readers to find out!)<br /><br />This book is a heartwarming,fun read! Noticed that my review is all about the characters? That's how awesome the author is in making and molding all her characters!^^<br /><br />Again,to my best buddy here on GoodReads,HAPPY BIRTHDAY! Wish you all the happiness this day,and all through out the years!^^</span>

  <span id="freeText8273295081878250991" style="display:none">Believe me. No one feels more sad about this rating than me. <br /><br /><i>On the Fence</i> was one of my most highly anticipated books of 2014. I love everything about Kasie West. Her books are usually ridiculously cute, have snarky characters and just speak to my soul. But not this one. This one was pretty un-Kasie West. The romance felt very unrealistic in a sense that it took the main character forever to figure out the love interest liked her. There’s only so much of that I can tolerate when it’s so completely obvious. However, <i>On the Fence</i>'s biggest issue was its predictability. I knew how the book would end right from the beginning and had long before figure out the SECRET everyone was keeping from the main character. This novel just fell really flat for me.</span>
